Actions That Do Not Break the Fast: Hanafi Rulings
Listing of six exceptions to fast invalidation with implicit proof from general principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six actions that do not invalidate the fast and explain the underlying Hanafi principle of 'al-sawm mimma dakhala'.

Core Idea
Only intentional entry of substance or intercourse breaks the fast; involuntary discharge, skin absorption, and negligible entry do not.

In this passage, the author lists specific actions that are often mistakenly thought to break the fast. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance based on the principle that fasting is breached by what enters the body deliberately, not by what exits or is applied externally. Understanding these exceptions helps avoid unnecessary doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that each listed action does not break the fast. The overall hukm for these actions is that they are permissible and do not affect the validity of the fast.
2
Classify each action
Group the actions: involuntary (wet dream), sensory (looking, kissing), external application (oil, kohl), and extraction (cupping). Recognize commonalities.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
The underlying rule is that the fast is only invalidated by something entering the body cavity (jawf) or brain through an open passage intentionally, or by sexual intercourse with ejaculation. None of these actions involve intentional intake of a substance.
See the principle 'al-sawm mimma dakhala la mimma kharaja'.
4
Note cross-madhhab differences
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider cupping makruh or hold that kohl breaks the fast if it reaches the throat. Understand that the Hanafi view is based on their usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۶۲] (۱۲) اگر سو گیا اور احتلام ہوا (۲) یا عورت کی طرف دیکھا اور انزال ہوا (۳) یا تیل لگایا (۴) یا پچھنا لگایا (۵) یا سرمہ لگایا (۶) یا بوسہ نام فاحتلم او نظر الى امرأته فانزل او ادهن او احتجم واكتحل او قبل لم يفطر
If he slept and had a wet dream, or looked at his wife and discharged, or applied oil, or cupped, or applied kohl, or kissed — he does not break his fast.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage lists six actions that do not invalidate the fast. The underlying principle is that the fast is only broken by something entering the body (dakhil) or through sexual intercourse with intentional discharge. Wet dreams, looking with discharge (without touching), applying oil (which absorbs through skin), cupping (blood extraction), applying kohl (substance that may reach the brain but is considered negligible), and kissing (without intentional discharge) are all exempt because they lack direct intentional entry of substance or do not constitute the act of intercourse. The Hanafi school relies on hadith and the general principle 'al-sawm mimma dakhala la mimma kharaja' (fasting is affected by what enters, not what exits).

Key Terms
احتلام (ihtilam): Nocturnal emission or wet dream; an involuntary discharge of semen during sleep.
احتجم (ihtajama): He cupped himself or received cupping; a therapeutic bloodletting.
اكتحل (iktahala): He applied kohl (antimony) to the eyes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Cupping (hijama)
B) Eating forgetfully
C) Kissing with intentional discharge
D) Applying oil

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that actions like wet dreams, looking with discharge, applying oil, cupping, kohl, and kissing do not invalidate the fast because they lack intentional entry of substance or direct sexual intercourse.

Discharge from Kissing/Touching: Qada Only, No Kaffarah
Ruling on intentional discharge from kissing/touching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting when discharge occurs from kissing or touching, and distinguish between qada and kaffarah obligations.

Core Idea
Intentional discharge breaks the fast but only requires makeup, not full expiation.

This lesson addresses a common scenario during fasting: kissing or touching one's spouse that leads to ejaculation. The text clearly distinguishes between the act itself and its consequence, specifying that while the fast becomes invalid, the penalty is limited to making up the day without the severe expiation required for intercourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering act
Recognize that the ruling applies only when kissing (qubla) or touching (lams) is done with desire and leads to discharge (inzal).
The act itself does not break the fast; only the discharge does.
2
Determine the hukm of the fast
Once discharge occurs intentionally, the fast becomes batil (invalid).
This is analogous to intercourse in its effect of nullifying the fast.
3
Identify the required compensation
The text states 'alayhi al-qada' — he must make up that day of fasting.
Qada is making up one fast for one day.
4
Note the absence of kaffarah
The text explicitly says 'wa la kaffarah 'alayhi' — no expiation is required.
Kaffarah is a severe penalty (fasting 60 days or feeding 60 poor) reserved for deliberate intercourse during fasting.
5
Understand the reasoning
The Urdu commentary explains the general principle: the fast is only broken by entry of something into the body or by intercourse. Discharge alone without entry does not break, but here it is considered a deliberate act that breaks because it results from intentional stimulation.
The proof is qiyas: discharge from kissing/touching is like intercourse in nullifying the fast but differs in the penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۶۳] (۱۳) فان انزل بقبلة او لمس فعليه القضاء ولا كفارة عليه. لیا تو روزہ نہیں ٹوٹا۔ (۱) روزہ ٹوٹتا ہے کسی چیز کے پیٹ کے اندر یا دماغ کے اندر جانے سے یا جماع کرنے سے، اوپر کی صورتوں میں نہ جماع کرنا پایا گیا اور نہ پیٹ میں یاد ماغ میں کوئی چیز گئی ہے اس لئے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
So if he discharges by kissing or touching, then upon him is qada (makeup) and no kaffarah upon him.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between mere kissing/touching (which does not break the fast) and the same act when it results in discharge (mani or madhi). If discharge occurs, the fast is invalidated because it amounts to intentional ejaculation, which is analogous to sexual intercourse in its effect on fasting. However, since no actual intercourse took place, the penalty is only qada (making up one day) and not kaffarah (which is reserved for deliberate intercourse). The Urdu explanation reaffirms that the fast is only broken by entry of something into the body or by sexual intercourse; discharge alone without entry does not break, but if it results from kissing/touching, it is considered a deliberate act that breaks the fast.

Key Terms
انزال (inzal): Ejaculation; emission of semen (or madhi) resulting from sexual arousal.
قبلة (qubla): Kissing; specifically here, kissing with sexual desire.
لمس (lams): Touching; here, touching with sexual desire that may lead to discharge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only kaffarah, no qada

Key Takeaway
Intentional discharge from kissing/touching invalidates the fast and requires qada, but does not require kaffarah.

Ruling on Kissing While Fasting
Ruling with proof on kissing during fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing while fasting and explain the distinction between qada and kaffarah when ejaculation occurs.

Core Idea
Kissing is allowed if one is safe from desire; if ejaculation occurs, only qada is required, not kaffarah.

The act of kissing during Ramadan fasting raises questions about its validity and required compensation. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, which distinguishes based on one's control over desire and the consequences if ejaculation occurs. Through prophetic traditions and scholarly statements, we will see why kaffarah is not imposed even when the fast is broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two-part ruling
The matn states two rulings: kissing is permissible (no harm) if one is safe from his desire, and disliked if not safe. Note the condition that changes the ruling.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on control.
2
Locate the proofs
The passage cites three pieces of evidence: an athar from al-Hasan and Qatada, a hadith from Maymuna, and a hadith from Abu Hurayra. Each supports a different aspect of the ruling.
These are all ahad hadiths, but together they form a coherent position.
3
Analyze the consequence of ejaculation
If kissing leads to ejaculation, the fast is broken (futir) according to the hadith from Maymuna. However, the athar from Qatada specifies only qada (one day fasting) is required, not kaffarah. Understand the reasoning: kaffarah is dropped due to doubt (shubuhat) because the act is not full intercourse.
This is unique to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may require kaffarah.
4
Understand the condition for dislike
The hadith from Abu Hurayra shows the Prophet permitting an old man but forbidding a young man. This indicates that the ruling becomes disliked (makruh tanzih) for those who cannot control their desire, especially the youth.
The dislike is due to the risk of falling into sin, not because the act itself is inherently bad.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a fasting husband who is elderly and confident of his control: kissing is permissible. For a young man who fears arousal: it is disliked. If despite his control, ejaculation happens unexpectedly: fast is broken, qada required, no kaffarah.

There is no harm in kissing if one is safe from himself, and it is disliked if he is not safe. Since complete intercourse in form and meaning was not found, kaffarah is not obligatory. Because kaffarah is dropped due to doubts. But the form of intercourse was found and he had a role in emission of semen, so qada is obligatory. (2) There is an athar from al-Hasan regarding a man who kisses during the day in Ramadan... Qatada said: If the gushing fluid comes out of him, then he only has to fast one day. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...) (2) From Maymuna, the freed slave of the Prophet ﷺ, that the Prophet ﷺ was asked about a fasting person who kissed, so he said: He broke his fast. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...) This athar and hadith indicate that if kissing results in ejaculation, the fast is broken, but kaffarah is not necessary. There is no harm in kissing if one is in control of himself. The hadith and reason have already passed in issue no. 12. Kissing is disliked if one does not trust himself. (1) If he is young and does not trust himself, then kissing while fasting is disliked because there is danger that he may fall into intercourse. For that reason, if one is not in control of himself, kissing is disliked. (2) There is a hadith from Abu Hurayra that a man asked the Prophet ﷺ about touching (direct contact) for a fasting person, and he permitted him. Then another came and he forbade him. The one he permitted was an old man, and the one he forbade was a young man. (c) (Abu Dawud...) The reason for forbidding in the hadith was that he did not have control over himself. Therefore it will be disliked. Footnote: (a) al-Hasan was asked about a man who kisses during the day in Ramadan... Qatada said: If the gushing fluid comes out of him, then he has nothing except to fast one day. (b) The Prophet ﷺ was asked about a fasting person who kissed, and he said: The fast is broken.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This is a ruling statement followed by proof. The passage addresses kissing (قبلة) during fasting. The matn states two rulings: it is permissible (no harm) if one is safe from desire, and disliked if not safe. The commentator then explains: the reason kaffarah is not required even if ejaculation occurs is because kaffarah is dropped in cases of doubt (شبہات); here, the act is not full intercourse in form and meaning. However, qada (making up the fast) is required because the form of intercourse was present and the person contributed to the emission. The proof includes an athar from al-Hasan and Qatada stating that if ejaculation occurs from kissing, only one day of fasting is required (qada, not kaffarah). Also, a hadith from Maymuna states that kissing breaks the fast. The commentator then elaborates: kissing is disliked for a young person who cannot control his desire, citing the hadith of Abu Hurayra where the Prophet permitted an old man but forbade a young man. The footnote translates and summarizes these proofs. The lesson establishes the Hanafi position: kissing is mubah (permissible) if safe, makruh tanzihan (disliked) if not safe; if it leads to ejaculation, the fast is broken and qada is required, but no kaffarah.

Key Terms
القبلة (al-qubla): Kissing, specifically on the lips or face, during fasting.
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a broken fast by fasting another day.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast by intercourse, eating, or drinking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) The fast is broken and both qada and kaffarah are required.

Key Takeaway
Kissing during fasting is allowed for those who can control their desire; if it leads to ejaculation, the fast is broken, but only qada (not kaffarah) is required.

Ruling on Vomiting While Fasting
Ruling with proof on vomiting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vomiting during fasting and apply the distinction between intentional and unintentional vomiting.

Core Idea
Unintentional vomiting does not break the fast; intentional vomiting does, but only qada is required, no kaffarah.

Vomiting during Ramadan can cause confusion about whether the fast is broken. The Hanafi school provides a clear distinction based on intentionality and amount, supported by a hadith from Abu Hurayra. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on: vomiting during a fast. The ruling differs based on whether vomiting is involuntary (fast valid) or intentional (fast invalid, qada required).
Intentional vomiting is considered a mufsid (invalidator) if it fills the mouth.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Hurayra: 'Whoever is overcome by vomiting has no qada; whoever intentionally vomits, let him make it up.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud, classified as ahad (single-transmitter), so it is zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses 'فليس عليه قضاء' (no qada) to show the fast remains valid for unintentional vomiting. The imperative 'فليقض' (let him make it up) indicates the fast is broken for intentional vomiting, requiring qada.
No kaffarah is required because the act is not considered eating or drinking.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that any amount of intentional vomit breaks the fast, based on the absolute wording of the hadith. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf require a mouthful. The relied (mufta bihi) position is that only a mouthful breaks the fast.
This difference affects cases where a small amount is induced unintentionally or intentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ذرعه القيئ لم يفطر وان استقاء عامدا ملأ فمه فعليه القضاء. اگر کسی کو خود بخود قے آگئی تو روزہ نہیں ٹوٹا اور اگر تے جان بوجھ کر کی منہ بھر کر تو اس پر قضا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة ان النبي الله قال من ذرعه القيئ فليس عليه قضاء ومن استقاء عمدا فليقض (و) (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی من استقاء عمد ص ۱۵۳ نمبر ۷۲۰ وابوداؤد شریف، باب الصائم یستقیع عامد ا ص ۳۳۱ نمبر ۲۳۸۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خود بخود تھے ہوئی تو روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ کوئی چیز نکلی ہے داخل نہیں ہوئی ہے۔ لیکن جان کر قے باہر نکالی اور کی تو چونکہ ان کو قے کرنے میں دخل ہے اس لئے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ حاشیہ : (د) آپ نے فرمایا جس کو قے آگئی ہو اس پر قضا نہیں ہے اور جس نے قے کی جان کر تو وہ قضا کرے۔ آئندہ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں مطلق قے کرنے سے روزہ ٹوٹنے کا حکم ہے اس لئے تھوڑی قے بھی ہوتو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ کفارہ لازم اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ با ضابطہ کھانا کھانا نہیں پایا گیا۔
And if he is overcome by vomiting, he does not break his fast; and if he intentionally vomits a mouthful, then qada is upon him. If someone vomits unintentionally, the fast is not broken; and if he intentionally vomits a mouthful, then qada is upon him. There is a hadith from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever is overcome by vomiting, there is no qada upon him; and whoever intentionally vomits, let him make it up.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that if vomiting occurs unintentionally, the fast is not broken because something came out, not entered. But if he intentionally brings out vomit, then since he had a role in it, the fast is broken. Footnote: (d) He said: Whoever is overcome by vomiting has no qada, and whoever intentionally vomits, let him make it up. Further, Imam Muhammad says that the hadith gives an absolute ruling that vomiting breaks the fast, so even a small amount of vomit breaks the fast. Kaffarah is not required because organized eating is not found.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof regarding vomiting (قيء) during fasting. The matn states: unintentional vomiting does not break the fast; intentional vomiting (mouthful) breaks the fast and requires qada. The commentator provides a hadith from Abu Hurayra to this effect. The reasoning: in unintentional vomiting, something exits the body, nothing enters, so the fast remains valid. Intentional vomiting involves active expulsion, thus breaking the fast. The commentator adds that Imam Muhammad holds that any amount of intentional vomit breaks the fast (the matn specifies 'mouthful' but the hadith is general). No kaffarah is required because the act does not constitute eating. The footnote (د) summarizes the hadith. This lesson establishes the Hanafi position: unintentional vomiting does not nullify the fast; intentional vomiting does, with qada required. There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the minimum amount (mouthful vs. any amount).

Key Terms
القيء (al-qay'): Vomiting; the expulsion of stomach contents through the mouth.
ذرعه (dhara'ahu): Overcome by; involuntary vomiting.
استقاء (istaqā'a): To intentionally induce vomiting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a fasting person intentionally vomits less than a mouthful?
A) The fast is broken and qada is required.
B) The fast is broken and kaffarah is required.
C) The fast is not broken and no compensation is needed.
D) The fast is not broken but qada is required as a precaution.

Key Takeaway
Unintentional vomiting does not break the fast; intentional vomiting of a mouthful breaks the fast and requires qada, but no kaffarah.

Swallowing Non-Edible Objects While Fasting
Ruling with proof on swallowing non-edible objects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on swallowing non-edible objects while fasting and explain the proof from the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
Swallowing non-food breaks the fast (qada) but no kaffarah — form vs. substance.

What happens if a fasting person deliberately swallows a pebble or a date pit? These are not food, yet the fast becomes invalid. This lesson explains why the Hanafi school requires qada but not kaffarah, and traces the proof to an athar about chewing gum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is deliberately swallowing a non-edible object (pebble, iron, date pit). The ruling: the fast breaks (mufsid) and qada is wajib; kaffarah is not wajib.
2
Understand the rationale: form vs. reality
In form (surah), the act is eating because something enters the stomach intentionally. In reality (haqiqah), it is not food. The fast breaks because of the form, but kaffarah is not due because of the reality.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Locate the dalil: athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i
The proof is an athar (report) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: he permitted chewing gum as long as it does not enter the throat. The mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite meaning) indicates that if it enters the throat, the fast breaks.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
4
Apply qiyas to other non-edible objects
The ruling for gum is extended by qiyas (analogy) to all objects that are not normally eaten as food or medicine: pebbles, iron, date pits, etc.
The illa (effective cause) is that the substance is not nutritive or medicinal.
5
Confirm the mandatory compensation
Since the substance is not food, kaffarah is not wajib. Only qada (making up one day) is required. If the substance were food (e.g., bread), both qada and kaffarah would be necessary.
Kaffarah is specific to deliberate, voluntary eating of normal food.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ابتلع الحصاة او الحديد او النواة افطر وقضى. کسی نے کنکری نگلی یا لوہا یا گٹھلی نگلی تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور قضا کرے۔ اگر چہ یہ چیزیں کھانے کی نہیں ہیں لیکن صورۃ کھانا ہے اس لئے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ لیکن حقیقت میں یہ چیزیں کھانے کی نہیں ہے اس لئے مکمل کھانا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے کفارہ لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اثر میں یہ الفاظ ہیں۔ عن ابراهیم انه رخص في مضغ العلك للصائم مالم يدخله حلقه (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبه اسم من رخص فی مضغ العلک للصائم ج ثانی ص ۲۹۷، نمبر ۹۱۷۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ملک چبائے اور حلق میں نہ جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے جس کا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہوگا کہ اگر حلق میں گیا تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اور علک دانت صاف کرنے کے لئے چبانے کی چیز ہے۔ عام طور پر غذا یا دوا کے طور پر کھانے کی چیز نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی پر ان تمام چیزوں کو قیاس کیا جائے جو عام طور پر غذا یا دوا کے طور کھانے کی چیز نہیں ہے۔ الحصاة : کنکری۔ النواة : گٹھلی۔
And whoever swallows a pebble, or iron, or a date pit, he breaks his fast and must make it up. If someone swallows a pebble, or iron, or a date pit, the fast will break and he must make it up. Although these things are not edible, in form they are eating, so the fast breaks. But in reality they are not food, so complete eating is not found, therefore kaffarah is not obligatory. (2) There is an athar with these words: from Ibrahim that he permitted chewing gum (ʿulak) for a fasting person as long as it does not enter his throat. (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...) This athar indicates that if one chews gum and it does not go down the throat, there is no harm; the opposite meaning is that if it enters the throat, the fast breaks. And gum is chewed for cleaning teeth; it is not generally eaten as food or medicine. And upon this is analogized all things that are not generally eaten as food or medicine. al-hasah: pebble. al-nawa: date pit.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on swallowing non-edible objects. The matn states that swallowing a pebble, iron, or date pit breaks the fast and requires qada. The commentator explains: these things are not food, so in reality they are not intended for nourishment, but in form the act is like eating. Therefore, the fast is invalid because something entered the stomach intentionally. However, since it is not food, kaffarah (expiation) is not required; only qada is necessary. The proof comes from an athar (effect of Ibrahim) regarding chewing gum: it is permitted as long as it is not swallowed. By extension (qiyas), any non-edible, non-medicinal substance swallowed intentionally breaks the fast and requires qada. The text defines 'al-hasah' as pebble and 'al-nawa' as date pit. This lesson highlights the Hanafi principle that the fast is broken by deliberate ingestion of any substance, even if not food, but kaffarah is only for specific nutritive acts.

Key Terms
الحصاة (al-hasah): A small stone or pebble.
النواة (al-nawa): A date pit or seed.
العلك (al-ʿulk): Chewing gum, used for cleaning teeth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Qada only.
C) Kaffarah only.
D) Both qada and kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
Swallowing non-edible objects intentionally breaks the fast and requires qada but not kaffarah; the proof is from the athar of Ibrahim and qiyas.

Ruling on Intercourse, Eating, and Drinking While Fasting
Ruling with proof on acts requiring both qada and kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three acts that require both qada and kaffarah during a Ramadan fast and explain the proof from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Deliberate intercourse, eating, or drinking in Ramadan require both qada and kaffarah.

This lesson addresses the most serious invalidators of a Ramadan fast that necessitate not only making up the day (qada) but also a heavy expiation (kaffarah). The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith and analogical reasoning, specifies three acts: intercourse in either passage, and consuming any nourishing or medicinal substance. Understanding this ruling is crucial for every fasting Muslim to avoid these major breaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts that require kaffarah
The matn lists three acts: intercourse in either of the two passages, eating something nourishing, and drinking something medicinal. Note the specific wording 'ma yutaghaddha bihi' and 'ma yutadawa bihi'.
2
Understand the primary proof (dalil naqli)
The hadith of the man who had intercourse in Ramadan; the Prophet ordered kaffarah (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor). This is the foundation.
3
Trace the extension by qiyas
Eating and drinking are analogized to intercourse because both are deliberate violations of the fast with full intention. The common ila is the intentional breaking of the fast in a major way.
4
Recognize the Hanafi specificity
Kaffarah is restricted to these three acts. Other acts that break the fast (e.g., swallowing a pebble, intentional vomiting) require only qada, not kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جامع عامدا في احد السبيلين او اكل او شرب ما يتغذى به او يتداوى به فعيله القضاء (والكفارة). کسی نے جماع کیا جان بوجھ کر دو استوں میں سے ایک میں یا کھایا یا پیا ایسی چیز جس سے غذا حاصل کی جاتی ہو یا اس سے دوا کی جاتی ہو تو اس پر قضا ہے اور کفارہ ہے۔ ی شرمگاہ میں یا پاخانہ کے راستہ میں روزے کی حالت میں جان بوجھ کر جماع کیا تو قضا اور کفارہ دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔ ان دونوں مقامات پر شہوت کاملہ ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے روزہ بھی ٹوٹے گا اور کفارہ بھی لازم ہو گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ان ابا هریر وقال بينما نحن جلوس عند النبى الله اذ جاءه رجل فقال يا رسول الله هلکت قال مالک قال وقعت على امرأتي وانا صائم فقال رسول الله الا الله هل تجد رقبة تعتقها قال لا قال فهل تستطيع ان تصوم شهرين متتابعين قال لا قال فهل تجد اطعام ستين مسكينا قال لا قال فمكث الخ (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا جامع فی رمضان ولم یکن له شی ، فتصدق علیه فلیکفر ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۹۳۶ وابوداؤد شریف ، کفارة من اتی اہلہ فی رمضان ص ۳۳۲ نمبر ۲۳۹۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان کے روزے میں جماع کر کے روزہ توڑے تو اس پر کفارہ لازم ہے (۳) اور اسی پر کھانے پینے کو قیاس کیا جائے کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی جان بوجھ کر روزہ توڑا گیا ہے۔ حاشیہ : (ب) اس درمیان کے ہم حضور کے پاس بیٹھے ہوئے تھے اچانک ایک آدمی آیا اور کہنے لگا اے اللہ کے رسول ! میں ہلاک ہو گیا۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا ہوا؟ کہا میں نے روزے کی حالت میں اپنی بیوی سے جماع کر لیا۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا تمہارے پاس غلام ہے جس کو آزاد کر سکو؟ انہوں نے کہا نہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم طاقت رکھتے ہو کہ دو ماہ مسلسل روزے رکھو؟ انہوں نے کہا نہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا کھانا ہے کہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھلا ؤ؟ انہوں نے کہا نہیں۔
And whoever intentionally has intercourse in either of the two passages, or eats or drinks something nourishing or medicinal, upon him is qada (and kaffarah). If someone intentionally has intercourse in either the front or the back passage, or eats or drinks something from which nourishment is derived or medicine is made, then upon him is qada and kaffarah. He has intercourse in the private part or the anus while fasting intentionally; then qada and kaffarah are both required. In both places, complete desire occurs, so the fast breaks and kaffarah is required. (2) There is a hadith from Abu Hurayra: While we were sitting with the Prophet ﷺ, a man came and said: O Messenger of Allah, I am destroyed! He said: What is the matter? He said: I had intercourse with my wife while fasting. The Prophet ﷺ said: Do you have a slave to free? He said: No. He said: Can you fast two consecutive months? He said: No. He said: Can you feed sixty poor people? He said: No. Then he sat... (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that if one breaks the fast by intercourse during Ramadan, kaffarah is required. (3) And upon this, eating and drinking are analogized, because in that case also the fast is broken intentionally. Footnote: (b) The same story in Urdu summary.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof covering the major invalidators of a Ramadan fast that require both qada and kaffarah. The matn specifies: intentional intercourse in either the front or back passage, or eating/drinking anything that is nourishing or medicinal. The commentator explains that intercourse in either passage (vagina or anus) results in complete desire, thus both qada and kaffarah are required. The primary proof is the well-known hadith of the man who had intercourse with his wife during Ramadan; the Prophet ordered kaffarah (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor). The commentator then notes that eating and drinking are analogized (qiyas) to intercourse because they also involve deliberate breaking of the fast. The footnote gives a translation/paraphrase of the hadith. This lesson establishes that for these fundamental acts, both qada and kaffarah are obligatory. The Hanafi position is that kaffarah is only for these specific acts (intercourse, eating, drinking) when done intentionally in Ramadan.

Key Terms
الجماع (al-jima'): Sexual intercourse, specifically here including both front and back passages.
السبيلين (al-sabilayn): The two passages: the front (vulva) and the back (anus).
ما يتغذى به (ma yutaghaddha bihi): That which is taken as nourishment (food).
ما يتداوى به (ma yutadawa bihi): That which is used as medicine.

B) Intentional vomiting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that only three acts—intercourse, eating, and drinking—when done intentionally during a Ramadan fast, require both qada and kaffarah.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner
6 min
Swallowing Non-Nutritive Objects During Fasting: Fast Breaks, Qada Only
Ruling on swallowing pebble, iron, or date seed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intentionally swallowing non-nutritive substances while fasting and explain why kaffarah is not required.

Core Idea
Swallowing a pebble, iron, or date seed breaks the fast but does not require kaffarah.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding fasting: what happens if a fasting person intentionally swallows an object that is not normally considered food or medicine, such as a pebble, a piece of iron, or a date seed. The text provides the ruling and the underlying reasoning, including an important analogy to chewing gum. By the end, you will understand the difference between qada (make-up) and kaffarah (expiation) in this context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is intentionally swallowing a non-nutritive object (pebble, iron, or date seed) while fasting. According to the Hanafi school, this act invalidates the fast (the fast becomes fasid) and requires qada (make-up fast), but kaffarah is not due.
The ruling is clear from the matn: 'afṭara wa qaḍā' (he breaks the fast and makes it up).
2
Locate the primary proof
The text cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: he permitted chewing gum for the fasting person as long as it does not enter the throat. This implies that if it enters the throat, the fast breaks. Although the athar is from a tabi'i, it serves as a basis for analogy.
The athar is used to establish that any substance entering the throat intentionally invalidates the fast.
3
Trace the qiyas reasoning
The ruling on gum is extended to other non-nutritive substances (pebble, iron, date seed) because the effective cause (illa) is that the substance is not normally eaten for nutrition or medicine. Thus, swallowing any such substance intentionally breaks the fast.
The qiyas is based on the shared illa: lack of normal nutritional/medicinal value.
4
Explain why kaffarah is not required
Kaffarah is only obligatory for breaking the fast by consuming actual food, drink, or engaging in sexual intercourse in a manner that involves nutrition or natural gratification. Non-nutritive objects are not considered 'food' or 'drink', so only qada is necessary.
The distinction between qada and kaffarah hinges on whether the substance is normally consumed for sustenance or medicine.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
For example, a person intentionally swallows a small piece of paper or a coin while fasting. The same ruling applies: the fast breaks, qada required, no kaffarah. This illustrates the broad principle: any non-nutritive object entering the stomach intentionally invalidates the fast.
The ruling is consistent across all non-nutritive objects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل) ۳۵۷
كتاب الصوم
۵۶۷] (۱۷) ومن ابتلع الحصاة او الحديد او النواة افطر وقضى [۵۶۸](۱۸) ومن جامع عامدا في احد السبيلين او اكل او شرب ما يتغذى به او يتداوى به فعيله القضاء ائندہ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں مطلق قے کرنے سے روزہ ٹوٹنے کا حکم ہے اس لئے تھوڑی قے بھی ہوتو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ کفارہ لازم اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ با ضابطہ کھانا کھانا نہیں پایا گیا۔
[۵۶۷] (۱۷) کسی نے کنکری نگی یا لوہایا گٹھلی نگی تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور قضا کرے۔
اگر چہ یہ چیزیں کھانے کی نہیں ہیں لیکن صورۃ کھانا ہے اس لئے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ لیکن حقیقت میں یہ چیزیں کھانے کی نہیں ہے اس لئے مکمل کھانا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے کفارہ لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اثر میں یہ الفاظ ہیں۔ عن ابراهیم انه رخص في مضغ العلك للصائم مالم يدخله حلقه (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته اسم من رخص فی مضغ العلک للصائم ج ثانی ص ۲۹۷، نمبر ۹۱۷۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ملک چبائے اور حلق میں نہ جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے جس کا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہوگا کہ اگر حلق میں گیا تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اور علک دانت صاف کرنے کے لئے چبانے کی چیز ہے۔ عام طور پر غذا یا دوا کے طور پر کھانے کی چیز نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی پر ان تمام چیزوں کو قیاس کیا جائے جو عام طور پر غذا یا دوا کے طور کھانے کی چیز نہیں ہے۔ الحصاة : کنکری۔ النواة : گٹھلی۔
حاشیہ : (الف) ابراہیم سے منقول ہے کہ انہوں نے روزہ دار کو ملک چبانے کے بارے میں رخصت دی جب تک کہ وہ حلق میں داخل نہ ہو جائے (ب ) اس درمیان کے ہم حضور کے پاس بیٹھے ہوئے تھے اچانک ایک آدمی آیا اور کہنے لگا اے اللہ کے رسول ! میں ہلاک ہو گیا۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا ہوا؟ کہا میں نے روزے کی حالت میں اپنی بیوی سے جماع کر لیا۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا تمہارے پاس غلام ہے جس کو آزاد کر سکو؟ انہوں نے کہا نہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم طاقت رکھتے ہو کہ دو ماہ مسلسل روزے رکھو؟ انہوں نے فرمایا کہ نہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا کیا کھانا ہے کہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھلا ؤ؟ انہوں نے کہا نہیں۔
And whoever swallows a pebble, or iron, or a date seed, he breaks the fast and must make it up. Imam Muhammad says that the hadith absolutely states that vomiting breaks the fast, so even a small amount of vomit breaks the fast. Kaffarah is not obligatory because the act of eating is not fully established. ... The effect: from Ibrahim that he permitted chewing gum for the fasting person as long as it does not enter his throat. This effect implies that if it enters the throat, the fast breaks. Gum is for cleaning teeth, not food. And by analogy, all things not normally eaten or used as medicine. Hashiya: (a) It is narrated from Ibrahim that he permitted the fasting person to chew gum as long as it does not enter his throat. (b) While we were sitting with the Prophet, a man came and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am destroyed!' He asked, 'What happened?' The man said, 'I had intercourse with my wife while fasting.' He asked, 'Do you have a slave to free?' He said no. He asked, 'Can you fast two consecutive months?' He said no. He asked, 'Can you feed sixty poor people?' He said no.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn and its commentary. The ruling states that swallowing a pebble, iron, or date seed breaks the fast and requires qada (make-up fast). The commentator explains that even though these are not food, the act of swallowing them is considered eating in form, so the fast breaks. However, since they are not nutritive, kaffarah is not required. The commentary also cites an effect from Ibrahim (the teacher of the early Kufan school) that chewing gum is permissible as long as it is not swallowed, indicating that anything that reaches the throat invalidates the fast. This is applied by analogy to all non-nutritive substances.

Key Terms
الحصاة (al-hasah): A pebble or small stone.
النواة (al-nawah): A date seed or pit.
القضاء (al-qada): To make up a missed fast on another day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on intentionally swallowing a date seed while fasting in Ramadan according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fast is valid, no qada.
B) Fast breaks, qada and kaffarah required.
C) Fast breaks, only qada required.
D) Fast is invalid, no qada needed.

Key Takeaway
Swallowing a non-nutritive object intentionally breaks the fast and requires qada, but not kaffarah, because it is not considered eating or drinking for nutrition.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
10 min
Kaffarah for Breaking the Fast: Intercourse, Eating, and Drinking
Combined ruling with proof and cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for breaking the fast by intercourse or eating/drinking, and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Intentional breaking of the fast by any nutritive means requires qada and kaffarah – the same as zihar.

This lesson addresses one of the most consequential rulings in Hanafi fiqh of fasting: the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) when a person intentionally breaks the Ramadan fast. The text covers three distinct scenarios – intercourse in the two passages, eating/drinking nutritive substances, and intercourse outside the two passages – and establishes that the kaffarah structure is identical to that of zihar. Additionally, the commentary engages with both cross-madhhab (Shafi'i) and intra-Hanafi (a narration from Abu Hanifa) disputes, highlighting the centrality of hadith evidence and qiyas in Hanafi istidlal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts that trigger kaffarah
From matn (18): intentional intercourse in al-sabilayn (front or back passage) or eating/drinking anything nutritive/medicinal. Note that 'intentional' means deliberate, not forgetful or coerced.
Al-sabilayn is a key term – both passages are included in the majority Hanafi view.
2
Locate the primary dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The hadith of Abu Huraira (the man who broke his fast) is cited. The Prophet commanded kaffarah without specifying the manner of breaking, implying generality. The Hanafi school argues the command covers any intentional iftar.
The hadith has zanni thubut and dalala, yet it is the basis for the ruling.
3
Trace the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts kaffarah to intercourse only, arguing that the hadith's incident involved intercourse. The Hanafi response: a separate hadith (al-Daraqutni) mentions a man who ate, and the Prophet still commanded kaffarah, and qiyas also supports the extension.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Shafi'i requires only qada for eating; Hanafi requires qada+kaffarah.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A narration from Abu Hanifa holds that intercourse in the anal passage does not require kaffarah, analogizing to the absence of hadd punishment. The mufta bihi is the majority view that both passages require kaffarah.
This shows the internal diversity of the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the rule to non-standard scenarios
Matn (20) clarifies that intercourse between thighs (outside the two passages) with ejaculation breaks the fast but requires only qada, not kaffarah. This is derived by qiyas awla from the hadith on kissing (which also breaks the fast).
The decisive factor is the absence of 'sabil' (passage) and the lesser intensity of shahwa.

۵۶۸] (۱۸) ومن جامع عامدا في احد السبيلين او اكل او شرب ما يتغذى به او يتداوى به فعيله القضاء
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاول
۳۵۸
كتاب الصوم
والكفار [۵۶۹] (۱۹) والكفارة مثل كفارة الظهار [ ۵۷۰] (۲۰) ومن جامع فيما دون توڑ نا پایا گیا (۴) اس بارے میں مطلق حدیث ہے کہ کسی بھی طرح افطار کرے تو کفارہ لازم ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة ان رجلا افطر في رمضان فامره رسول الله الا الله ان يعتق رقبة او يصوم شهرين متتابعين او يطعم ستين سكينا الخ (الف) (ابو دا اد شریف، کفارة من اتی اصلہ فی رمضان ص ۳۳۲ نمبر ۲۳۹۲) دار قطنی ، باب القبلة للصائم ج ثانی ص۱۷۰ نمبر ۲۲۸۳ ۲۲۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کسی بھی طرح رمضان کا روزہ توڑا ہو چاہے کھا پی کر اس پر کفارہ لازم ہے۔ دارقطنی کی حدیث نمبر ۲۲۸۴ میں ان رجلا اكل في رمضان فامره النبي ان يعتق رقبة الخ کی عبارت ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھانے سے بھی کفارہ لازم
ہوگا۔
فائنده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف جماع سے تو ڑا ہو تو کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔ اور کھا پی کر تو ڑا ہو تو کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ صرف قضا لازم ہوگی۔ پہلی حدیث میں جماع کر کے توڑنے پر کفارہ لازم کیا گیا ہے۔ اور دوسری حدیث میں بھی اسی کا جز ہے اس لئے کھانے پینے سے توڑنے کو جماع پر قیاس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ناند امام ابو حنیفہ کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ پاخانہ کے مقام میں جماع کرنے سے کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں اتنی شہوت پوری نہیں ہوتی جتنی شرمگاہ میں ہوتی ہے (۲) اور جس طرح اس میں جماع کرنے سے حد لازم نہیں ہوتی اسی طرح کفارہ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ [۵۶۹] (۱۹) اور روزہ توڑنے کا کفارہ ظہار کے کفارہ کی طرح ہے۔ کفارہ ظہار غلام آزاد کرتا ہے، وہ نہ ہو تو ساٹھ روز مسلسل روزے رکھنا ہے، اور وہ نہ ہو سکے تو ساٹھ مسکین کو کھانا کھلانا ہے۔ رمضان کا روزہ توڑنے میں بھی یہی کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔
مسئلہ نمبر ۱۸ میں بخاری شریف کی حدیث گزری جس میں کفارہ کی یہ تفصیل موجود تھی۔ اسی سے کفارہ کی تفصیل لازم ہے۔ اور کفارہ ظہار کی تفصیل سورہ مجادلہ ۵۸ یت نمبر ۱۳ اور ۴ میں ہے۔
[۵۷۰] (۲۰) جس نے جماع کیا فرج کے علاوہ میں اور انزال ہوا تو اس پر قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں ہے۔
یہاں فرج سے مراد شرمگاہ اور پاخانہ کے راستے کے علاوہ ہے۔ اس لئے ان دونوں کے علاوہ جگہ مثلاران وغیرہ میں جماع کیا اور انزال ہوا تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور قضا لازم ہوگی ۔ کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان مقامات پر شہوت کا ملہ نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ميمونة مولاة النبي الله ان النبى الله الله سئل عن صائم قبل فقال افطر (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ٢٠ من كره القبلة للصائم ولم يرخص فیھاج ثانی ص ۳۱۷، نمبر ۹۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بوسہ لینے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا تو غیر فرج میں جماع کرے اور انزال ہو جائے تو بدرجہ اولی روزہ ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اعلی درجہ کی حرکت ہوئی (۲) اثر میں ہے ان ابن مسعود قال في القبلة للصائم قولا
حاشیہ : (الف) ایک آدمی نے رمضان کے مہینہ میں روزہ توڑا تو حضور نے ان کو حکم دیا کہ غلام آزاد کرے، یا دو ماہ مسلسل روزے رکھے یا ساٹھ مسکین کو کھانا کھلائے ۔ (ب) آپ سے پوچھا گیا روزہ دار کے بارے میں کہ بوسہ لے لے تو کہا روزہ ٹوٹ گیا۔
And whoever has intercourse intentionally in one of the two passages, or eats or drinks something by which one is nourished or by which one is treated medically, then upon him is qada and kaffarah. ... [then matn for 19 and 20] ... The commentary: This matter has an absolute hadith that whoever breaks the fast in any way, kaffarah is required. The hadith of Abu Huraira: a man broke his fast in Ramadan, the Prophet commanded him to free a slave, fast two consecutive months, or feed sixty poor people. ... Imam Shafi'i holds that kaffarah is only for intercourse, not for eating or drinking. ... There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that intercourse in the anal passage does not require kaffarah because the passion is not as complete. ... [19] The kaffarah for breaking the fast is like the kaffarah of zihar. ... [20] Whoever has intercourse other than the two passages and has ejaculation, upon him is qada, not kaffarah.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage presents three rulings from the matn and their commentary. The first ruling (18) states that intentionally having intercourse in the front or back passage, or eating or drinking any nutritious or medicinal substance, breaks the fast and requires both qada and kaffarah. The commentator provides the hadith evidence from the incident of a man who broke his fast and the Prophet prescribed the kaffarah of freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor. The commentary also addresses a cross-madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi'i holds that kaffarah is only for intercourse, not for eating/drinking, but the Hanafi school argues that the hadith is general and includes any form of breaking the fast. Additionally, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: one narration from Abu Hanifa states that intercourse in the anal passage does not require kaffarah, based on analogy with the absence of hadd punishment. The second ruling (19) confirms that the kaffarah structure is identical to that of zihar. The third ruling (20) states that intercourse in other than the two passages (e.g., between thighs) with ejaculation breaks the fast and requires qada, but no kaffarah, using a hadith about kissing as evidence for qiyas awla.

Key Terms
السبيلين (al-sabilayn): The two passages (front and back) for intercourse; the defining location for triggering kaffarah.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation required for breaking a Ramadan fast intentionally; same as zihar kaffarah: free a slave, fast 60 days, feed 60 poor (sequential).
المتغذى (al-mutaghaddha): Something that provides nutrition; triggers kaffarah if consumed intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a person who intentionally eats a meal during a Ramadan fast?
A) Only qada
B) Qada and kaffarah
C) No qada
D) Only kaffarah

Key Takeaway
Intentional consumption of any nutritive substance during a Ramadan fast triggers both qada and the zihar-style kaffarah in the Hanafi school, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i position.

Sawm — Fasting

Kaffarah for Breaking Ramadan Fast
Ruling on kaffarah with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for breaking the Ramadan fast, identify the proof from hadith, and explain the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Kaffarah for breaking Ramadan fast is wajib for any intentional act—eating, drinking, or intercourse—based on absolute hadith.

This passage addresses a key ruling in the fiqh of sawm: the expiation (kaffarah) for intentionally breaking the fast of Ramadan. The Hanafi school, relying on general hadith evidence, holds that any intentional breach—whether by eating, drinking, or intercourse—requires the same three-step kaffarah as zihar. This lesson unpacks the proof and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Intentionally breaking the Ramadan fast. The ruling is that kaffarah is wajib.
Kaffarah here means the same expiation as for zihar.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Huraira in Abu Dawud and Darqutni: a man broke his fast (by any means) and the Prophet commanded kaffarah.
The hadith is ahad, thus the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command (amr) in the hadith indicates obligation. The word 'afṭara' is general, covering all forms of breaking the fast.
The Darqutni hadith explicitly includes eating, strengthening the generality.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kaffarah is only for intercourse, not eating/drinking. He argues that the hadith only mentions intercourse.
Shafi'i requires only qada for eating/drinking.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school follows the general hadith and the explicit Darqutni narration where a man ate. The mufta bihi is that any intentional break requires kaffarah.
The rare narration from Abu Hanifa on anal intercourse is not followed.

والكفارة مثل كفارة الظهار. اس بارے میں مطلق حدیث ہے کہ کسی بھی طرح افطار کرے تو کفارہ لازم ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة ان رجلا افطر في رمضان فامره رسول الله ان يعتق رقبة او يصوم شهرين متتابعين او يطعم ستين سكينا الخ (الف) (ابو داود شریف، كفارة من اتى اهله فی رمضان ص ۳۳۲ نمبر ۲۳۹۲) دار قطنی، باب القبلة للصائم ج ثانی ص۱۷۰ نمبر ۲۲۸۳ ۲۲۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کسی بھی طرح رمضان کا روزہ توڑا ہو چاہے کھا پی کر اس پر کفارہ لازم ہے۔ دارقطنی کی حدیث نمبر ۲۲۸۴ میں ان رجلا اكل في رمضان فامره النبي ان يعتق رقبة الخ کی عبارت ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھانے سے بھی کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ فائنده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف جماع سے توڑا ہو تو کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔ اور کھا پی کر توڑا ہو تو کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ صرف قضا لازم ہوگی۔ پہلی حدیث میں جماع کر کے توڑنے پر کفارہ لازم کیا گیا ہے۔ اور دوسری حدیث میں بھی اسی کا جز ہے اس لئے کھانے پینے سے توڑنے کو جماع پر قیاس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ناند امام ابو حنیفہ کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ پاخانہ کے مقام میں جماع کرنے سے کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں اتنی شہوت پوری نہیں ہوتی جتنی شرمگاہ میں ہوتی ہے اور جس طرح اس میں جماع کرنے سے حد لازم نہیں ہوتی اسی طرح کفارہ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور روزہ توڑنے کا کفارہ ظہار کے کفارہ کی طرح ہے۔ کفارہ ظہار غلام آزاد کرتا ہے، وہ نہ ہو تو ساٹھ روز مسلسل روزے رکھنا ہے، اور وہ نہ ہو سکے تو ساٹھ مسکین کو کھانا کھلانا ہے۔ رمضان کا روزہ توڑنے میں بھی یہی کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ مسئلہ نمبر ۱۸ میں بخاری شریف کی حدیث گزری جس میں کفارہ کی یہ تفصیل موجود تھی۔ اسی سے کفارہ کی تفصیل لازم ہے۔ اور کفارہ ظہار کی تفصیل سورہ مجادلہ آیت نمبر ۳ اور ۴ میں ہے۔
And the expiation is like the expiation of zihar. About this, there is an absolute hadith that if one breaks the fast in any way, expiation is obligatory. In the hadith: from Abu Huraira that a man broke his fast in Ramadan, so the Messenger of Allah commanded him to free a slave, or fast two consecutive months, or feed sixty poor people... (a) (Abu Dawud Sharif, chapter on expiation for one who has intercourse in Ramadan, p. 332 no. 2392; Darqutni, chapter on kissing for the fasting person, vol. 2 p. 170 nos. 2283-2284). This hadith indicates that breaking the fast of Ramadan in any way, even by eating or drinking, requires expiation. In Darqutni's hadith no. 2284, the wording is 'a man ate in Ramadan, so the Prophet commanded him to free a slave...' meaning that eating also necessitates expiation. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i says that only if the fast is broken by intercourse does expiation become obligatory, but if broken by eating or drinking, expiation is not obligatory; only qada is necessary. The first hadith made expiation obligatory for breaking by intercourse, and the second hadith is part of the same, so breaking by eating and drinking is not analogized to intercourse. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that expiation is not obligatory for intercourse in the anus because the desire is not as complete as in the vagina, and just as hadd is not obligatory for such intercourse, so too expiation is not obligatory. The expiation for breaking the fast is like the expiation for zihar. The expiation for zihar is to free a slave; if he cannot, then to fast sixty consecutive days; if he cannot, then to feed sixty poor people. Similarly, for breaking the fast of Ramadan, the same expiation is obligatory. In issue number 18, the Bukhari hadith that passed contained this detail of expiation. From it the detail of expiation is deduced, and the detail of expiation for zihar is in Surah Al-Mujadilah verses 3 and 4.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the expiation (kaffarah) for breaking the fast of Ramadan. The author states that the kaffarah is identical to that of zihar (a form of divorce). The proof is from multiple hadith, including one from Abu Huraira where a man broke his fast and the Prophet ordered one of three options: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor. The author also cites Darqutni's hadith where a man ate, also commanding expiation. The passage includes a fiqhi benefit (fa'idah) showing the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi'i holds that kaffarah applies only to breaking fast by intercourse, not by eating/drinking, whereas the Hanafi position (based on the absolute wording of the hadith) applies it to any intentional breaking. The author also mentions a rare (nadir) narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that anal intercourse does not necessitate kaffarah because it lacks full gratification, analogous to it not requiring hadd (fixed punishment). This narration is not the relied-upon position. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that any intentional breaking of the Ramadan fast (by eating, drinking, or intercourse) requires the same three-step kaffarah as zihar. The basis for the details of zihar kaffarah is Quran 58:3-4. The passage emphasizes that the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that any form of fast-breaking obligates kaffarah, contrary to Shafi'i, and the rare view of Abu Hanifa on anal intercourse is not followed.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for sinful acts, here specifically for intentionally breaking the Ramadan fast.
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce by comparing one's wife to a female relative, requiring expiation.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated fast on another day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required if someone intentionally eats during a Ramadan fast?
A) Only qada
B) Qada and kaffarah
C) Only kaffarah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires kaffarah (as in zihar) for any intentional break of the Ramadan fast, based on general hadith evidence.

Ruling on Intercourse Outside Genitals with Emission
Ruling on breaking fast by non-genital intercourse with emission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse outside the genitals with emission during fasting and explain why only qada is required, not kaffarah.

Core Idea
Intercourse outside genitals with emission breaks the fast, but only qada is required, not kaffarah.

The fast is a sacred act with specific conditions. Some acts, like genital intercourse, require both qada and kaffarah. But what about acts that are less severe? This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri clarifies that when a fasting person engages in intercourse in non-genital areas (e.g., between thighs) and emits semen, the fast is broken and only qada is obligatory. The ruling is derived from the hadith on kissing and applied through qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling in daily fasting scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intercourse (jima') in a place other than the genitals (faraj) accompanied by emission (inzal). The ruling is that the fast is broken and qada is required, but kaffarah is not.
Genitals here include the vagina and anus.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites a hadith from Maymuna that the Prophet (ﷺ) said about a fasting person who kisses: 'afṭara' (he broke his fast). This hadith is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
The hadith is ahad (single transmission), so it establishes zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The Prophet's statement that kissing breaks the fast establishes that any act short of genital intercourse can break the fast when it involves desire and likely emission. The author applies qiyas awla (greater reason): if kissing (which is less intense) breaks the fast, then intercourse outside the genitals with emission (which is more intense) certainly breaks the fast.
The illa (effective cause) is the occurrence of emission from an act of desire.
4
Note the limitation to qada only
The author clarifies that kaffarah is not required because the act is not full genital intercourse. Kaffarah is reserved for the most severe form of fast-breaking (jima' in the genitals with penetration). The evidence is the athar of Ibn Mas'ud which states that for kissing with emission, only qada is required, and this is the Hanafi position (عندنا).
This distinction is consistent with the principle that kaffarah is only for the specific act mentioned in the Quran and hadith.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that only qada is wajib; no kaffarah. There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf mentioned.
The author's phrase 'and this is according to us' (وهذا عندنا) indicates the authoritative stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۷۰] (۲۰) جس نے جماع کیا فرج کے علاوہ میں اور انزال ہوا تو اس پر قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں ہے۔ یہاں فرج سے مراد شرمگاہ اور پاخانہ کے راستے کے علاوہ ہے۔ اس لئے ان دونوں کے علاوہ جگہ مثلاران وغیرہ میں جماع کیا اور انزال ہوا تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور قضا لازم ہوگی۔ کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان مقامات پر شہوت کا ملہ نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ميمونة مولاة النبي ان النبي سئل عن صائم قبل فقال افطر (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ٢٠ من كره القبلة للصائم ولم يرخص فیھا ج ثانی ص ۳۱۷، نمبر ۹۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بوسہ لینے سے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا تو غیر فرج میں جماع کرے اور انزال ہو جائے تو بدرجہ اولی روزہ ٹوٹے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اعلی درجہ کی حرکت ہوئی۔ اثر میں ہے ان ابن مسعود قال في القبلة للصائم قولا شديدا يعنى يصوم يوما مكانه و هذا عندنا فيه اذا قبل فانزل (ج) (سن للبيهقی، باب وجوب القضا على من قبل فانزل ج رابع ص ۱۳۹۵ نمبر ۸۱۰۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرج کے علاوہ میں جماع کرنے سے منی نکل جائے تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور قضا واجب ہے، کفارہ نہیں۔ حاشیہ : (ب) آپ سے پوچھا گیا روزہ دار کے بارے میں کہ بوسہ لے لے تو کہا روزہ ٹوٹ گیا۔ (ج) حضرت عبداللہ ابن مسعود نے روزہ دار کے لئے بوسہ لینے کے بارے میں سخت بات کہی۔ یعنی اس کی جگہ ایک روزہ رکھے گا اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک اس وقت ہے جب بوسہ لے اور انزال ہو جائے۔
(20) And whoever has intercourse in other than the vagina (faraj) and has emission, then upon him is qada and no expiation. Here faraj means other than the vagina and anus. So if one has intercourse in places other than these two, like between thighs, etc., and emission occurs, the fast is broken and qada is necessary. There is no expiation because these places are not the full seat of desire. In the hadith: from Maymuna, the freed slave of the Prophet, that the Prophet was asked about a fasting person who kissed, and he said: 'He has broken his fast.' (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 2 p. 317 no. 9426). From this hadith it is known that kissing breaks the fast; so by greater reason, intercourse in other than the genitals with emission breaks the fast, because this is an even greater act. There is an athar (tradition) from Ibn Mas'ud who said a severe statement about kissing for the fasting person, meaning he should fast one day in its place, and this is according to us when he kisses and has emission. (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, vol. 4 p. 1395 no. 8106). From this athar it is known that intercourse in other than the genitals with emission breaks the fast and qada is obligatory, not expiation.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the effect of intercourse in a place other than the vagina or anus when accompanied by emission. The author states that only qada (making up the fast) is required, not kaffarah. The reason is that such places (e.g., between thighs) do not provide the same level of gratification as the genitals, so the act is less severe. The proof is by analogy (first to kissing, then to a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud specifically about kissing with emission requiring qada only). The author argues that since kissing (which is less intense) breaks the fast, then intercourse in non-genital areas (which is more intense) also breaks the fast, but still only qada because the full kaffarah is reserved for genital intercourse. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that kaffarah is only for the most severe form of fast-breaking.

Key Terms
فرج (faraj): Here means the genital area, specifically the vagina and anus.
انزال (inzal): Emission of semen, which breaks the fast in this context.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed fast (required here).
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation (fasting 60 consecutive days or feeding 60 poor) required for intentional genital intercourse during Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qada and kaffarah
B) Only qada
C) The fast is valid
D) Only kaffarah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intercourse outside the genitals with emission requires only qada, not kaffarah, because kaffarah is reserved for full genital intercourse.

No Expiation for Breaking Non-Ramadan Fasts
Ruling with proof on kaffarah for non-Ramadan fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for non-Ramadan fasts and explain the basis using the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is exclusive to Ramadan; for any other fast, only qada is required.

This passage clarifies a common confusion: not every broken fast requires expiation (kaffarah). The ruling distinguishes between the sacred obligation of Ramadan and other fasts (voluntary, qada, or vow). The proof comes directly from a hadith where the Prophet commanded only qada for a broken voluntary fast, without any mention of kaffarah. This lesson will walk through the ruling, its evidence, and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breaking a fast that is not the Ramadan fast (e.g., voluntary, qada, or vow). The ruling is that only qada (making up the day) is required; no kaffarah is necessary.
This is the explicit statement of the text: 'No expiation for breaking a fast other than in Ramadan.'
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith from Aisha (ra) where the Prophet said: 'Fast one day in its place.' This hadith is recorded in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
The hadith does not mention kaffarah, showing it was not required.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'صوما مكانه يوما آخر' (fast one day in its place) implies only qada. The absence of any added penalty indicates that kaffarah is not part of the ruling for non-Ramadan fasts.
Hanafi usul: the silence of the text on an additional action (kaffarah) indicates it is not required.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
All major schools (Hanafi, Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree that kaffarah is specifically for Ramadan fasts. There is no legitimate disagreement on this point.
This is considered muttafaq alayh among the schools.
5
Apply the ruling
For any non-Ramadan fast, whether voluntary, qada, or nadhr, the consequence is only qada. No kaffarah, no other penalty.
Example: if someone breaks a voluntary fast on a Monday, they must make it up later but do not pay kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۷۱] (۲۱) رمضان کے علاوہ کے روزے توڑنے میں کفارہ نہیں ہے۔ (۱) رمضان کا روزہ فرض ہے اس کے علاوہ کا روزہ فرض نہیں ہے۔ اور نہ اس کی اتنی اہمیت ہے۔ اس لئے رمضان کے علاوہ کا روزہ توڑ دے تو صرف قضا لازم ہوگی۔ کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں جو کفارہ کا ذکر ہے وہ رمضان کے روزے توڑنے میں ہے دوسرے روزے میں نہیں۔ اس لئے دوسرے روزے کو اس پر قیاس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ غیر رمضان میں روزہ توڑنے سے کفارہ لازم نہیں ہو گا صرف قضا لازم ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عائشة قالت ... فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صوما مكانه يوما آخر (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رای علیه القضاء ص ۳۴۰ نمبر۲۴۵۷ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ایجاب القضاء علیہ، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۷۳۵ ) اس حدیث میں نفلی روزہ توڑنے پر صرف قضا لازم کی گئی ہے۔
(21) There is no expiation for breaking a fast other than in Ramadan. (1) The fast of Ramadan is obligatory; a fast other than it is not obligatory, nor does it have such importance. Therefore, if one breaks a non-Ramadan fast, only qada is necessary; kaffarah is not necessary. (2) The mention of kaffarah in the hadith is only for breaking the fast of Ramadan, not for other fasts. Hence other fasts are not analogized to it, and kaffarah is not required. The evidence is the hadith from Aisha: ... the Messenger of Allah said: 'Fast one day in its place.' (Abu Dawud no. 2457; Tirmidhi no. 735). In this hadith, only qada is required for breaking a voluntary fast.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that kaffarah (expiation) is only for intentionally breaking an obligatory fast of Ramadan. For any other fast—whether voluntary (nafl), qada, or vow (nadhr)—breaking it only requires qada (making up the day). The reason is that kaffarah is a severe penalty reserved for the sanctity of Ramadan. The proof is from a hadith where the Prophet told Aisha to fast one day in place of a broken voluntary fast, without any mention of kaffarah. This distinguishes the ruling from Ramadan.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or broken fast on another day.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast, involving freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Kaffarah only
C) Both qada and kaffarah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah is exclusive to Ramadan; for all other fasts, only qada is wajib.

Ruling on Enema, Nose/Ear Drops, and Wound Dressing Breaking Fast
Ruling that inserting substances into body orifices breaks the fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that any substance entering the stomach or brain via an opening (enema, nose/ear drops, deep wound treatment) breaks the fast and requires qada, and identify the proof from the athar of Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah.

Core Idea
Any substance entering the stomach or brain via any opening breaks the fast—fasting is about what enters, not what exits.

Many assume only eating and drinking through the mouth can break the fast. However, Hanafi fiqh extends the ruling to any substance that enters the body cavity through an opening, including medical procedures. This lesson explains the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and ruling
List the specific actions mentioned: enema, nose drops, ear drops, and medicine applied to deep wounds (jā'ifah and āmmah). The ruling is that the fast is broken (fasid) and requires qada.
The common element is that a substance reaches the stomach or brain.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the athar from Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah: 'الصوم مما دخل وليس مما خرج' (Fasting is about what enters, not what exits). Additional narrations from al-Thawri and Ata' support the ruling on enema.
This athar is recorded in Bukhari and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar explicitly defines fasting by what enters the body. Therefore, any intentional entry of a substance through an opening (including medical portals) invalidates the fast. The key is reaching the body cavity (stomach or brain).
This is a zanni dalil but relied upon in the school.
4
Note the consequence
The passage does not mention kaffarah, only qada. This distinguishes these acts from intentional eating/drinking, which requires both qada and kaffarah (in Ramadan).
The enema with wine example clarifies that the hadd penalty is not applied because it is not drunk in the usual manner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۷۲] (۲۲) جس نے حقہ لیا یا ناک میں دوا ڈالی یا کان میں قطرہ ٹپکا یا یا پیٹ کے زخم کی دوا کی یا دماغ کے زخم کی تر دوا کی اور وہ پیٹ تک پہنچ گئی یا دماغ تک پہنچ گئی تو روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ کوئی بھی کھانے پینے کی چیز یا دوا کی چیز دماغ تک یا آنت تک پہنچ جائے تو اس سے روزہ ٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔ اوپر کی صورتوں میں منفذ اور سوراخ کے ذریعہ دو یا پانی آنت اور دماغ تک پہنچ رہے ہیں اس لئے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے قال ابن عباس و عكرمة الصوم مما دخل وليس مما خرج (بخاری شریف، باب الحجامة والقين للصائم ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۱۹۳۸ سنن بیھقی ، باب الافطار بالطعام و بغیر الطعام اذا از درده عامدا او بالسعوط والاحتقان و غیر ذلك مما یدخل جوفه با ختیارو ج رابع ص ۲۶۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی چیز داخل ہو جائے تو اس سے روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا اور داخل ہونے کا مطلب پیٹ میں یا دماغ میں داخل ہونا ہے جو اصل ہیں۔ حقنہ کے بارے میں اثر موجود ہے عن الثوري قال يفطر الذي يحتقن بالخمر ولا يضرب الحد (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحقنة في رمضان والرجل یصیب اہلہ ج رابع ص ۱۹۹ نمبر ۷۴۷۸ ) عن عطاء كره ان يستدخل الانسان شيئا في رمضان بالنهار فان فعل فليبدل يوما ولا يفطر ذلك اليوم (ج) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الحقيه في رمضان والرجل یصیب اہلہ ص ۱۹۹ نمبر ۷۴۷ )
(22) Whoever uses an enema, or puts medicine in the nose, or drops something in the ear, or treats a deep stomach wound, or treats a deep brain wound, and it reaches the stomach or brain, then the fast is broken. Any food, drink, or medicine that reaches the brain or intestines breaks the fast. In the above cases, through an opening or hole, medicine or water reaches the intestines and brain, so the fast is broken. There is an athar (tradition) from Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah: 'Fasting is related to what enters, not what exits.' (Bukhari, chapter on cupping and vomiting for the fasting person, p. 260 no. 1938; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, vol. 4 p. 261). From this athar, it is learned that if something enters, it breaks the fast. 'Entering' means entering the stomach or brain, which are the main cavities. Regarding enema, there is an athar from al-Thawri: 'He who uses an enema with wine breaks his fast but is not flogged with the hadd penalty.' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, vol. 4 p. 199 no. 7478). And from Ata: 'It is disliked for a person to insert something during the day in Ramadan. If he does, he should replace one day [i.e., fast another day] and not break his fast that day.' (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, vol. 4 p. 199 no. 7474).
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on when the fast is broken by substances entering the body through openings other than the mouth. The author lists: enema, nose drops, ear drops, and medicine applied to deep wounds that reach the stomach or brain. The common principle is that any substance (food, medicine) that enters the body cavity (stomach or brain) from an external opening breaks the fast. The proof includes an athar from Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah that 'fasting is about what enters, not what exits,' and specific traditions about enema from al-Thawri and Ata. Note: For non-food substances, qada is required but no kaffarah, unless the substance is nutritional. The hadith about enema with wine specifies that while it breaks the fast, it does not incur the hadd penalty for intoxication because it is not consumed in the usual way.

Key Terms
حقنة (huqnah): Enema: injecting liquid into the rectum.
جائفة (jā'ifah): A deep wound that reaches the body cavity (stomach or brain).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, does using an enema break the Ramadan fast?
A) Yes, and requires kaffarah
B) Yes, and requires only qada
C) No, it does not break the fast
D) It is permissible without any issue

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: any substance entering the stomach or brain via an opening (including enema, drops, wound treatments) invalidates the fast and requires qada.

Tasting Food While Fasting: Ruling and Dislike
Ruling that tasting with the mouth does not break the fast but is disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasting food while fasting, identify the evidence from Ibn Abbas, and explain why the act is disliked.

Core Idea
Tasting with the mouth does not break the fast but is disliked due to risk of swallowing.

In this lesson, we examine a common scenario for a fasting person: tasting food to check its flavour. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that the fast remains valid as long as nothing is swallowed, but cautions against unnecessary tasting because of the risk of accidental swallowing. We will explore the proof from a companion's statement and the rationale behind the disliked ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and note the main ruling: 'Whoever tastes something with his mouth does not break his fast.' Identify the act (tasting with the tongue) and the hukm (the fast is sahih, not invalidated).
2
Understand the reason for the ruling
The fast is not broken because the substance does not reach the stomach. Tasting involves only the tongue; swallowing is required to invalidate the fast. Why does the Hanafi school hold this view? Trace the logic: the fast is broken only when something enters the stomach.
This aligns with the general principle that the fast is nullified by the arrival of food or drink in the stomach.
3
Analyse the dislike (karahah)
The text states that tasting is 'makruh' without need. Why is it disliked if it does not break the fast? Because there is a risk that some drops may accidentally slip down the throat. The dislike is tanzihi (slight), not tahrimi (prohibited).
This caution protects the integrity of the fast.
4
Locate the evidence
The passage cites Ibn Abbas's statement: 'There is no harm in the fasting person tasting something, meaning broth and the like.' Identify the type of evidence (Qawl Sahabi) and its weight (zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala in this context).
How does this statement prove the ruling? The phrase 'no harm' indicates that the fast is not affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذاق شيئا بفمه لم يفطر ويكره له ذلك [۵۷۴] (۲۴) اگر کسی نے منہ سے کچھ چکھ لیا تو روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا لیکن یہ مکروہ ہے۔ صرف منہ سے چکھنے سے پیٹ میں کوئی چیز نہیں گئی اس لئے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا لیکن ممکن ہے کہ کبھی کوئی چیز پیٹ میں چلی جائے اور روزہ ٹوٹ جائے اس لئے بغیر ضرورت کے ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال لا بأس ان يتطاعم الصائم بالشيء يعنى المرقة و نحوها (الف) ( سنن بیتی ، باب الصائم يذوق شياج رابع ص ۲۳۵، نمبر ۸۲۵۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شور بہ وغیرہ چکھنے سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا بشرطیکہ پیٹ میں کوئی چیز نہ جائے۔
And whoever tastes something with his mouth does not break his fast, and it is disliked for him to do so. (24) If someone tastes something with their mouth, the fast is not broken, but this is disliked. Merely tasting with the mouth does not cause anything to go into the stomach, so the fast is not broken. But it is possible that something might go into the stomach, causing the fast to break; therefore, doing so without need is makruh. The athar from Ibn Abbas: 'There is no harm in the fasting person tasting something, meaning broth and the like.' This indicates that tasting broth etc. does not break the fast as long as nothing reaches the stomach.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on tasting food or liquid with the tongue while fasting. The fast remains valid because tasting does not involve swallowing; the substance does not reach the stomach. However, the action is makruh tanzihi (disliked) because there is a risk that some particles may accidentally slip down the throat. The evidence is the statement of Ibn Abbas permitting the fasting person to taste broth and similar items, confirming that tasting does not invalidate the fast. The Hanafi ruling balances the preservation of the fast's validity with caution against potential nullification.

Key Terms
ذاق (dhāqa): To taste with the tongue without swallowing.
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but should be avoided to protect the integrity of the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fasting person tastes soup to check its saltiness, what is the ruling?
A) His fast is broken immediately
B) His fast is valid but the action is disliked without necessity
C) His fast is broken only if he swallows
D) His fast is valid and the action is recommended

Key Takeaway
Tasting with the tongue does not invalidate the fast, but it is disliked due to the risk of accidental swallowing, so unnecessary tasting should be avoided.
