And if he delayed it until the next Ramadan entered, he fasts the second Ramadan and makes up the first after it, and there is no fidyah upon him. From this hadith it is understood that making up with intervals or consecutively is permissible. However, fasting consecutively to quickly discharge the obligation is better. There is a hadith from Abu Huraira: the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has fasts of Ramadan to make up, let him fast them consecutively and not break them.' (Dar Qutni). From this hadith it is understood that he should not break them but fast consecutively and complete them quickly. [582] (32) Explanation: He kept delaying the qada of Ramadan until the second Ramadan came. So he will fast the second Ramadan, and make up the first after it, and there is no fidyah upon him. For a person who had some qada fasts from Ramadan but kept delaying them until the next year's Ramadan came, he will now fast the current Ramadan and make up the previous year's fasts after this Ramadan. (1) The previous year's fasts are already qada. If he delays the second year, they will also become qada. Therefore, he should fast the second year's fasts on time and then make up the first year's fasts later. (2) There is an athar from Abu Huraira: 'A man became ill during Ramadan, then recovered, but did not make up until the next Ramadan came. So he should fast the one that came, then make up the other, and feed a poor person for each day.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that he will first fast the second Ramadan, and then make up the first Ramadan's fasts. And fidyah is not obligatory because after qada is due, whenever he makes it up it is still qada, so no fidyah. The mention of feeding a poor person for each day in the athar is as a recommendation (istihbab), not as an obligatory fidyah.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on a person who delays making up missed Ramadan fasts until the next Ramadan arrives. The ruling is clear: one must first fast the current Ramadan (which is obligatory on time) and then make up the previous missed fasts afterward. No fidyah (expiation) is required for the delay, because the missed fasts remain a debt to be made up whenever possible. The passage cites a hadith recommending consecutive fasting to discharge the obligation quickly, and an athar from Abu Huraira that supports the sequence (current Ramadan first, then qada) and suggests feeding a poor person as a meritorious act, not an obligation. The author clarifies that the feeding mentioned in the athar is istihbabi (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, as found in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up an obligatory act of worship that was missed or invalidated; here specifically missing Ramadan fasts.
فدیہ (fidyah): A compensatory payment (feeding a poor person) for missed fasts when one cannot make them up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person delays making up missed Ramadan fasts until the next Ramadan, what is the Hanafi ruling on fidyah?
A) He must pay fidyah for each delayed day.
B) No fidyah is required, but he must fast the current Ramadan first and then make up the missed fasts.
C) He must fast the current Ramadan and also pay fidyah for the missed fasts.
D) He is excused and need not make up the missed fasts at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position is that one must prioritize the current Ramadan fasts and then make up past missed fasts without any fidyah for the delay.

Pregnant and Nursing Women: Qada vs Fidyah
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on pregnant/nursing women's fasts, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Pregnant/nursing women make up missed fasts later; the elderly pay fidyah—they cannot make up.

Islamic law accommodates genuine hardship. For a pregnant or nursing woman who fears for her child, fasting may be harmful. Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars agree she may break the fast, but they differ on what comes next: must she later make up the days (qada) or does she compensate by feeding the poor (fidyah) and skip qada? This passage from a Hanafi work lays out the school's position and rebuts the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: pregnant/nursing women who fear for their child break fast, make up later (qada), no fidyah.
This is the mufta bihi ruling of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such women pay fidyah (feed a poor person each day) and do not make up missed fasts.
Both schools agree the women are excused from fasting; the difference is on the substitute.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the evidence cited by Shafi'i: the athar of Sa'id ibn Jubayr and the general verse (2:184) about fidyah for those who cannot fast.
The Shafi'i reading applies the verse to pregnant/nursing women directly.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the verse applies only to those who can never make up (shaykh fani). Pregnant/nursing women are like the sick/traveler—temporarily unable, so qada is sufficient. The athar of Ibn Abbas is more specific and says they make up, no fidyah.
The Hanafi response uses specificity (takhsis) to prioritize Ibn Abbas over Sa'id ibn Jubayr.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi women must make up missed fasts after Ramadan; Shafi'i women pay fidyah and do not make up.
This difference affects millions of women every year.

(33) The pregnant and nursing woman, if they fear for their children, they break the fast and make up, and there is no fidyah upon them. Because these women can make up later, so no fidyah upon them. They will make up the fasts with delay. But the elderly (shaykh fani) has no hope of recovery, so he gives fidyah. However, because there is fear of losing the child, these women are in the category of the sick and traveler, so they break now and make up later. (2) There is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik: '... Allah has removed half the prayer from the traveler and removed fasting from the pregnant and nursing woman.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that pregnant and nursing women are not required to fast, and they will make up later and not give fidyah. The evidence is this athar from Ibn Abbas: 'The pregnant and nursing woman breaks fast in Ramadan and makes up fasting and does not feed (i.e., no fidyah).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba? Actually it says Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that she does not give fidyah but makes up. Because she has the ability to make up later, she will make up. Fidyah only applies when she cannot make up in her lifetime, like the elderly. Imam Shafi'i says that pregnant and nursing women give fidyah and do not make up. Their evidence is the athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: 'The pregnant woman who is in her (Ramadan) month and the nursing woman who fears for her child break fast and each feed a poor person for each day, and there is no qada upon them.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). And their evidence is also the verse: 'And those who can only with hardship are to feed a poor person.' (2:184). From the verse it is understood that those without ability give fidyah. The verse includes the elderly. But according to the saying of Ibn Abbas, pregnant and nursing women are also included: Ibn Abbas said: 'The verse was a concession for the elderly man and woman who can still fast (with difficulty) to break and feed a poor person, and the pregnant and nursing women when they fear.' (Abu Dawud). From this athar it is understood that the pregnant and nursing also give fidyah for each day instead of fasting.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on pregnant and nursing women who fear harm to their child if they fast. The Hanafi position is that they should break the fast and later make up the missed days, with no fidyah (monetary compensation). The reasoning is that they are like the sick or traveler: temporarily unable to fast but able to make up later. Only the perpetually incapable (like the very elderly) must give fidyah. The author then engages in an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that such women give fidyah and do not make up the fasts, based on an athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr and the general verse about fidyah. The Hanafis counter with an athar from Ibn Abbas that explicitly says they make up and do not feed (i.e., no fidyah), and note that the verse about fidyah applies to the elderly, not to those who can later make up. The passage also includes a hadith from Anas about the concession for pregnant and nursing women. The Hanafi position is thus: qada only, no fidyah. This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حامل (hamil): A pregnant woman who fears harm to her child if she fasts.
مرضع (murdi'): A nursing woman who fears harm to her child if she fasts.
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): An extremely old person who has no hope of recovery and cannot fast at all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) She must make up the fasts later and does not pay any fidyah.
D) She is permanently excused and needs neither qada nor fidyah.

Key Takeaway
Pregnant and nursing women who fear for their child break fast and make up later; they do not pay fidyah, unlike the elderly who can never make up.

Fidyah for the Elderly Who Cannot Fast
Ruling on the very elderly who cannot fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an elderly person permanently unable to fast and apply the condition that fidyah replaces qada when no recovery is expected.

Core Idea
Permanent incapacity transforms the obligation from qada to fidyah.

The Quranic concession for the elderly (2:184) allows breaking the fast and paying fidyah. The Hanafi school specifies that this applies only when there is no hope of regaining strength. This lesson clarifies the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Name the act and its legal category
Identify the act as fidyah for missed fasts, which falls under the category of compensation (badal) in the chapter of sawm.
2
Identify the hukm level
Determine whether the fidyah is wajib, sunnah, or mubah. The imperative in the text indicates obligation.
Hanafi: fidyah is wajib, not fard, because the duty is a substitute and not the original fast.
3
List the conditions for this ruling
Extract from the text the conditions: the person must be extremely old (shaykh fani), unable to fast at all, and with no hope of recovery.
The condition of 'no hope' is implied by the term 'fani' (failing).
4
Specify the obligation and its comparator
The text states that the feeding is like that in kaffarat. This indicates the amount: half a sa‘ of wheat or one sa‘ of barley per day.
The exact measure is derived from other sources; the text draws an analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۸۴] (۳۴) والشيخ الفاني الذي لا يقدر على الصيام افطر ويطعم كل يوم مسكينا كما يطعم في الكفارات
(34) The very elderly (shaykh fani) who is unable to fast: he breaks the fast and feeds a poor person for each day, just as he feeds in expiations (kaffarat).
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This brief ruling states the Hanafi position for an elderly person who has no physical capacity to fast and no hope of recovery. Such a person is not required to fast, nor to make up the fasts later (since they cannot). Instead, they must pay fidyah, which is feeding one poor person for each missed day. The comparison to kaffarat (expiations) indicates that the amount of food given should be similar to that given in expiatory meals. This is an exception to the general rule that missed fasts must be made up; permanent incapacity transforms the obligation to fidyah. The ruling is based on the Quranic verse (2:184) and is agreed upon across schools.

Key Terms
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): An extremely old person who has no hope of regaining strength to fast.
کفارات (kaffarat): Expiatory payments or acts for transgressions; here the amount of food given as fidyah is compared to the food given in kaffarat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must make up the fasts later when able.
B) He must pay fidyah (feed a poor person) for each missed day.
C) He must pay a monetary penalty but not fast.
D) He is excused entirely with no obligation.

Key Takeaway
For the permanently elderly who cannot fast, fidyah replaces the obligation to fast or make up fasts.

Pregnant & Breastfeeding: Qada Only, No Fidyah
Dispute on fast compensation for pregnant/nursing women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for pregnant/breastfeeding women who miss Ramadan fasts and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by citing the respective proofs.

Core Idea
Pregnant/nursing women owe qada (make-up), not fidyah, because they can fast later.

When a pregnant or breastfeeding woman fears harm to herself or her child, she may break her Ramadan fast. But what is required afterward? Must she make up the fasts later (qada) or pay a ransom (fidyah)? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on this point. In this lesson, we examine the evidence behind each position and understand why the Hanafi school holds that only qada is required.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a pregnant/breastfeeding woman breaks fast and makes it up later; no fidyah.
This applies when she fears harm to herself or the child.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Locate the hadith and athar cited: the Prophet ﷺ said Allah removed fasting from them, and Ibn Abbas said they make up and do not feed.
The key athar is from Ibn Abbas in Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.
3
State the Shafi'i opposing position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that she pays fidyah for each missed day and does not make up the fast.
This is based on an athar of Sa'id ibn Jubayr and the verse of fidyah (2:184).
4
Identify the Shafi'i proof
Note the athar: Sa'id ibn Jubayr said she feeds a poor person per day and no qada. Also verse 2:184 is interpreted to include her.
The verse is general ('those who are able'), and Ibn Abbas included pregnant/nursing in its scope.
5
Understand the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response argues that the verse applies to those permanently unable (like the decrepit old man). Since pregnant/nursing women can fast later, they must make up, not pay fidyah. The athar of Ibn Abbas is preferred because it is more specific to their situation.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

They both break fast and make up, and there is no fidyah upon them. [584] (34) And the decrepit old man who cannot fast... Abdullah bin Ka'b narrated to me about fasting that Allah has removed half of the prayer from the traveler and removed fasting from the pregnant or nursing woman. The Prophet said 'both of them or one of them'. (a) (Tirmidhi...). From this hadith it is known that pregnant and nursing women do not have to fast. And later they will make up and will not give fidyah. The reason is this athar: Ibn Abbas said: The pregnant and nursing woman breaks fast in Ramadan and they both make up the fast and do not feed. (b) (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq...). From this athar it is known that she will not give fidyah but will make up. (2) Because she has the ability to make up later, so she will make up. Fidyah is only when she cannot make up for the rest of her life, like the decrepit old man who cannot make up fasts for the rest of his life. Imam Shafi'i says that the pregnant and nursing woman will give fidyah and will not make up. Their evidence is this athar: Sa'id bin Jubayr said: The pregnant woman in her month and the nursing woman who fears for her child - they both break fast and each feeds one poor person every day, and there is no making up upon them. (c) (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq...). From this athar it is known that the pregnant and nursing woman will feed one poor person for each day and will not make up. Their evidence is also this verse: 'And upon those who are able, a ransom of feeding a poor person' (Surah Baqarah 2:184). From the verse it is known that those who do not have ability will give fidyah. In this verse the decrepit old man is included. But according to Ibn Abbas's statement, pregnant and nursing are also included. From Ibn Abbas: 'And upon those who are able, a ransom of feeding a poor person' - he said: It was a concession for the very old man and very old woman who have the ability to fast that they break fast and feed a poor person for each day, and the pregnant and nursing when they fear. (e) (Abu Dawud...). From this athar it is known that the pregnant and nursing also give fidyah for each day's fast.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling for pregnant and breastfeeding women who fear hardship or harm to themselves or the child if they fast in Ramadan. The Hanafi position is that they break the fast and later make it up (qada) without paying fidyah (ransom). The key proof is the hadith that Allah removed fasting from the pregnant/nursing woman, and the athar of Ibn Abbas which states they make up and do not feed. The rationale is that they have the ability to make up later, unlike the decrepit old man who cannot. The Shafi'i position, presented here, is that they do not make up but instead pay fidyah for each missed day, based on the athar of Sa'id ibn Jubayr and the verse of fidyah. The Hanafi response implicitly argues that the verse applies to those permanently unable, and the athar of Ibn Abbas specifies that pregnant/nursing only make up. The passage thus defends the Hanafi view against the Shafi'i evidence.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): A ransom or compensation paid by feeding a poor person for each missed fast, due by those who are permanently unable to fast.
قضا (qada): Making up missed obligatory fasts on later days after Ramadan.
حامل (hamil): A pregnant woman.
مرضعہ (murdi'ah): A breastfeeding woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a pregnant woman who breaks a Ramadan fast due to fear for herself do?
A) Pay fidyah and not make up the fast.
B) Make up the fast later and pay fidyah.
C) Make up the fast later with no fidyah.
D) Neither make up nor pay fidyah.

Key Takeaway
Pregnant and breastfeeding women break fast and make up later (qada) without fidyah, because they can fast after Ramadan.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner
6 min
Decrepit Old Man: Fidyah Instead of Fasting
Ruling on the elderly person permanently unable to fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the shaykh fani (permanently unable to fast), explain the proof from Quran and hadith, and calculate the required fidyah.

Core Idea
A permanently elderly person incapable of fasting pays fidyah and does not make up the fast.

This lesson addresses the shaykh fani, an extremely old person who has no hope of recovering the ability to fast. The Hanafi school rules that such a person breaks the fast during Ramadan and for each missed day must feed one poor person with half a sa' of wheat (or equivalent) as fidyah. The evidence is the verse in Surah Baqarah (2:184) interpreted by Ibn Abbas, along with the athar. Crucially, there is no requirement for qada because the inability is permanent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of person
Recognize that the shaykh fani is an elderly person who is permanently unable to fast due to old age or a chronic condition, with no hope of recovery. This is distinct from a temporary illness journey, etc.
The permanent inability is key.
2
Extract the ruling
From the text, the ruling is that he breaks the fast (if he had intended) and for each missed day he must pay fidyah by feeding one poor person. He does not make up the fast.
The ruling is wajib, based on the verse.
3
Analyze the dalil
The text cites the Quranic verse (Surah Baqarah 2:184) which allows a 'ransom' for those who can bear it. The athar from Ibn Abbas confirms that this applies to the shaykh fani and specifies the amount as half a sa' of wheat per day.
This is a clear dalil naqli.
4
Determine the fidyah amount and method
The fidyah is half a sa' of wheat (or equivalent in value or other staple food) per missed fast, given to one poor person. It can be given at the end of Ramadan or distributed as each day is missed.
Other schools differ on amount, but Hanafi is half sa' wheat.
5
Distinguish from related cases
Contrast with the pregnant/breastfeeding woman who is able to fast later (qada required) or the ill person who may recover (qada after recovery). The shaykh fani's case is permanent, hence only fidyah.
The distinction is based on hope of recovery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۸۴] (۳۴) اور شیخ فانی جو روزے پر قدرت نہ رکھتا ہو افطار کرے گا۔ اور ہر دن کے بدلے ایک مسکین کو کھانا کھلائے گا جیسا کہ کفارات میں کھلاتے ہیں۔
(۱) او پر آیت گزر گئی جس میں تھا کہ جو طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو وہ ہر روز کے بدلے میں کفارہ ایک مسکین کا کھانا دے۔ اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس انه كان يقرأها وعلى الذين يطيفونه ويقول هو الشيخ الكبير الذى لا يستطيع الصيام فيفطر ويطعم عن كل يوم مسكينا نصف صاع من حنطة (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الشيخ الكبير ج رابع ص ۲۲۱ نمبر ۷۵۷۴ ربخاری شریف ، باب قولہ تعالی ایا ما معدودات فمن کان منکم مریضا الخ ج ثانی ص ۶۴۷ کتاب التفسیر، نمبر ۴۵۰۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شیخ فانی قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ اور ہر دن کے بدلے آدھا صاع گیہوں مسکین کو فدیہ دے گا۔
(34) And the decrepit old man who has no ability to fast will break fast. And for each day he will feed one poor person, just as he feeds in kaffarat. (1) The verse has passed which said that whoever does not have ability, he gives the kaffara of feeding one poor person for each day. There is an athar: Ibn Abbas used to recite it as 'And upon those who can bear it' and said: It is the very old person who cannot fast, so he breaks fast and feeds for each day half a sa' of wheat for a poor person. (a) (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq... Bukhari...). From this athar it is known that the decrepit old man will not make up. And for each day he will give half a sa' of wheat as fidyah to a poor person.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning the shaykh fani, a person so old that he is permanently unable to fast. The ruling is clear: he breaks the fast during Ramadan and for each missed day, he must pay fidyah by feeding one poor person half a sa' of wheat (or equivalent). The proof is the verse of fidyah (Surah Baqarah 2:184) and its interpretation by Ibn Abbas, who specifies that it applies to the very old. Importantly, there is no qada for such a person because the inability is permanent. The fidyah is similar to that in kaffarat (expiation) but is specific to missed fasts. This ruling is distinguished from the pregnant/breastfeeding case where qada is possible.

Key Terms
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): An extremely old person who is physically unable to fast and has no hope of recovery.
صاع (sa'): A unit of measure; half a sa' of wheat (approximately 1.5-2 kg) is the fidyah per missed fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the fidyah amount for one missed fast according to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage?
A) One sa' of dates
B) Half a sa' of wheat
C) One mudd of barley
D) A full meal

Key Takeaway
A person permanently unable to fast due to old age must pay fidyah (half sa' wheat per day) and is not required to make up the fasts.
